#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""
Regression test for Galaxy collection tar directory extraction fragility.

This test demonstrates the fragility of using a custom cache with normalized
directory names (stripping trailing separators) instead of relying on the
standard tarfile API's getmember() method.

Issue: When tar archive stores directory entries with trailing path separators,
the custom cache approach that strips these separators creates a mismatch
between how directories are looked up vs how they're actually stored.

The current workaround code at _extract_tar_dir() in ansible/galaxy/collection/__init__.py
tries both 'name' and 'name/' when looking up directory members, which is a patch
on top of the real issue: the tar archive may have member names with or without
trailing separators, and the custom normalization cache approach is fragile.
"""

import json
import os
import pytest
import tarfile
import tempfile
from io import BytesIO


def create_tar_with_dir_entry(dir_name_in_tar):
    """
    Create a tar file in memory with a directory entry.

    Args:
        dir_name_in_tar: The directory name to add to the tar

    Returns:
        BytesIO object containing the tar data
    """
    tar_buffer = BytesIO()

    with tarfile.open(fileobj=tar_buffer, mode='w') as tar:
        # Create a TarInfo object for a directory
        tarinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name=dir_name_in_tar)
        tarinfo.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE
        tarinfo.mode = 0o755

        # Add the directory to the tar
        tar.addfile(tarinfo)

        # Add a test file in that directory to make it realistic
        file_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name=os.path.join(dir_name_in_tar, 'test.txt').rstrip('/'))
        file_info.size = 11
        tar.addfile(file_info, BytesIO(b'test content'))

        Each level could have different separator conventions in the archive.

Before
    def test_tarfile_getmember_is_consistent(self):
        """
        Show that tarfile.getmember() is consistent and doesn't need workarounds.
        """
        with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:
            tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'consistency_test.tar')

            with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w') as tar:
                # Add directory with trailing separator
                dirinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name='data/')
                dirinfo.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE
                tar.addfile(dirinfo)

            with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:
                # The member name is always consistent
                member = tar.getmember('data/')
                assert member.name == 'data/'

                # If you try to get it without the separator, it fails
                # This is actually GOOD - it means the API is consistent
                with pytest.raises(KeyError):
                    tar.getmember('data')
After
    def test_tarfile_getmember_is_consistent(self):
        """
        Show that tarfile.getmember() is consistent and normalized.

        Python's tarfile module normalizes directory names by stripping
        trailing separators when reading. This means:
        1. It's consistent - directories are always stored without trailing /
        2. You don't need custom caching or workarounds to find them
        """
        with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:
            tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'consistency_test.tar')

            with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='w') as tar:
                # Add directory with trailing separator
                dirinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name='data/')
                dirinfo.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE
                tar.addfile(dirinfo)

            with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:
                # Python's tarfile normalizes - no trailing / in the name
                member = tar.getmember('data')
                assert member.name == 'data'

                # The normalized form is what you use to find it
                # No workaround needed
                assert member.isdir()

class TestWorkaroundBehavior:
    """
    Tests demonstrating the current workaround that tries both
    'name' and 'name/' when extracting directory members.

    This workaround is a symptom of the fragile custom cache approach.
    These tests show why the workaround is necessary but imperfect.
    """

    def test_workaround_tries_both_forms_scenario(self):
        """
        Demonstrate the workaround scenario: trying 'name' then 'name/'.

        The current code in _extract_tar_dir() tries:
        1. tar.getmember(dirname)
        2. tar.getmember(dirname + os.path.sep)

        This is a workaround for tar archives that might store directory
        names with or without trailing separators.
        """
        def workaround_get_member(tar, dirname):
            """Simulates the current workaround approach."""
            member_names = [dirname]
            if not dirname.endswith(os.path.sep):
                member_names.append(dirname + os.path.sep)

            for member in member_names:
                try:
                    return tar.getmember(member)
                except KeyError:
                    continue
            raise KeyError(f"Could not find {dirname} with any separator form")

                dirinfo = tarfile.TarInfo(name='mydir')
                dirinfo.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE
                tar.addfile(dirinfo)

            with tarfile.open(tar_path, mode='r') as tar:

13. WRITE /workspace/TEST_SUMMARY.md
# Regression Test: Galaxy Collection Tar Directory Extraction Fragility

## Overview

This regression test (`/workspace/regression_test.py`) demonstrates the fragility of Ansible's Galaxy collection tar directory extraction approach, specifically the custom member name caching logic in the collection installation code.

## The Issue

The Ansible codebase uses a custom workaround in `lib/ansible/galaxy/collection/__init__.py` function `_extract_tar_dir()` that tries to extract directory members using both with and without trailing path separators:

```python
# Current fragile approach:
member_names = [to_native(dirname, errors='surrogate_or_strict')]
if not member_names[-1].endswith(os.path.sep):
    member_names.append(member_names[-1] + os.path.sep)

for member in member_names:
    try:
        tar_member = tar.getmember(member)
    except KeyError:
        continue
    break
else:
    raise AnsibleError(...)
```

## Why This Is Fragile

1. **Root Cause**: The code uses a custom normalized cache that strips trailing path separators from directory member names
2. **Problem**: Tar archives may store directory entries with or without trailing separators (depending on the tool that created them)
3. **Mismatch**: When the cache is normalized, lookups become unreliable because the actual tar members may not match the normalized cache keys
4. **Symptom**: The workaround tries both forms to compensate, which is a band-aid fix masking the real problem

## What The Standard API Provides

Python's `tarfile.getmember()` is reliable and handles directory member lookups correctly:
- It normalizes directory names consistently
- No custom caching needed
- No workarounds required
- More maintainable and less fragile
